<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

								<div class="post-111 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-111">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>7.4 &#8212; Passing arguments by address</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on July 25th, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p>There is one more way to pass variables to functions, and that is by address.  <strong>Passing an argument by address</strong> involves passing the address of the argument variable rather than the argument variable itself.  Because the argument is an address, the function parameter must be a pointer.  The function can then dereference the pointer to access or change the value being pointed to.</p>
<p>Here is an example of a function that takes a parameter passed by address:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>

<p></p>
<p>The above snippet prints:</p>
<pre>
nValue = 5
nValue = 6
</pre>
<p>As you can see, the function foo() changed the value of nValue through the pointer parameter pValue.</p>
<p>Pass by address is typically used with dynamically allocated variables and arrays.  For example, the following function will print all the values in an array:</p>

<p></p>
<p>This program prints the following:</p>
<pre>
6
5
4
3
2
1
</pre>
<p>Note that the length of the array must be passed in as a parameter, because arrays don&#8217;t keep track of how long they are.  Otherwise the PrintArray() function would not know how many elements to print.</p>
<p>It is always a good idea to ensure parameters passed by address are not null pointers before dereferencing them.  Dereferencing a null pointer will typically cause the program to crash.  Here is our PrintArray() function with a null pointer check:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73f0d9b52969843141" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0017 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Advantages of passing by address:</p>
<ul>
<li>It allows us to have the function change the value of the argument, which is sometimes useful
<li>Because a copy of the argument is not made, it is fast, even when used with large structs or classes.
<li>We can return multiple values from a function.
</ul>
<p>Disadvantages of passing by address:</p>
<ul>
<li>Because literals and expressions do not have addresses, pointer arguments must be normal variables.
<li>All values must be checked to see whether they are null.  Trying to dereference a null value will result in a crash.  It is easy to forget to do this.
<li>Because dereferencing a pointer is slower than accessing a value directly, accessing arguments passed by address is slower than accessing arguments passed by value.
</ul>
<p>As you can see, pass by address and pass by reference have almost identical advantages and disadvantages.  Because pass by reference is generally safer than pass by address, pass by reference should be preferred in most cases.</p>
<p><strong>Passing by reference, address, and value is actually not so different</strong></p>
<p>Now that you understand the basic differences between passing by reference, address, and value, let&#8217;s complicate things by simplifying them. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
<p>In the lesson on <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/73-passing-arguments-by-reference/">passing arguments by reference</a>, we briefly mentioned that references are typically implemented by the compiler as pointers.  Because of this, the only real difference between pointers and references is that references have a cleaner but more restrictive syntax.  This makes references easier and safer to use, but also less flexible.  This also means that pass by reference and pass by address are essentially identical in terms of efficiency.</p>
<p>Here&#8217;s the one that may surprise you.  When you pass an address to a function, that <em>address</em> is actually passed by value!  Because the address is passed by value, if you change the value of that address within the function, you are actually changing a temporary copy.  Consequently, the original pointer address will not be changed!</p>
<p>Here&#8217;s a sample program that illustrates this.</p>

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0037 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Because pTempPtr receives a copy of the address of pPtr, even though we change pTempPtr, this does not change the value that pPtr points to.  Consequently, this program prints</p>
<pre>
565
</pre>
<p>Even though the address itself is passed by value, you can still dereference that address to permanently change the value at that address!  This is what differentiates pass by address (and reference) from pass by value.</p>
<p>The next logical question is, &#8220;What if we want to be able to change the address of an argument from within the function?&#8221;.  Turns out, this is surprisingly easy.  You just use pass the pointer itself by reference (effectively passing the address by reference).  You already learned that values passed by reference reflect any changes made in the function back to the original arguments.  So in this case, we&#8217;re telling the compiler that any changes made to the address of pTempPtr should be reflected back to pPtr!  The syntax for doing a reference to a pointer is a little strange (and easy to get backwards): <code>int *&amp;pPtr</code>.  However, if you do get it backwards, the compiler will give you an error.</p>
<p>The following program illustrates using a reference to a pointer.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b63601979461-6">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b63601979461-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">pTempPtr</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;nSix</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b63601979461-8">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b63601979461-9"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// This will print 6</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b63601979461-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pTempPtr</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b63601979461-11"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0012 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Note that you&#8217;ll also have to update the function prototype above main to account for the new prototype of SetToSix():</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73f0d9b6a482004684" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0d9b6a482004684-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0d9b6a482004684-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0d9b6a482004684-3">3</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b6a482004684-1"><span class="crayon-c">// Function prototype so we can define&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b6a482004684-2"><span class="crayon-c">// SetToSix below main()&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0d9b6a482004684-3"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">SetToSix</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;pTempPtr</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>When we run the program again with this version of the function, we get:</p>
<pre>
566
</pre>
<p>Which shows that calling SetToSix() did indeed change the address of pPtr!</p>
<p>So strangely enough, the conclusion here is that references are pointers, and pointer addresses are passed by value.  The value of pass by address (and reference) comes <em>solely</em> from the fact that we can dereference addresses to change the original arguments, which we can not do with a normal value parameter.</p>

		<p>Disadvantages of passing by address:</p>
<p>Because dereferencing a pointer is slower than accessing a value directly, accessing arguments passed by address is slower than accessing arguments passed by value.</p>
<p>Could that sentence possibly supposed to read as follows:</p>
<p>Because dereferencing a pointer is slower than accessing a value directly, accessing arguments passed by address is slower than accessing arguments passed by reference.</p>
<p>I would think (am assuming) that arguments passed by value would take the longest because they have to be copied.</p>
<p>[ It turns out that references are usually implemented by the compiler (under the hood) using pointers.  Consequently, references aren&#8217;t any faster than addresses.  They just have a nicer syntax, and are safer to use. -Alex ]</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		<p>I think I get it.  Passing by value is slow because it does a copy.  Passing by reference or address is basically the same thing, just different syntax.</p>
<p>[ Correct.  I&#8217;ve read that if you&#8217;re passing simple built-in variables by value, it can be as fast or faster than passing by reference or address.  Generally when we talk about passing by reference or address being faster, we&#8217;re talking about for compound types (eg. structs and classes). -Alex ]</p>

class="crayon-t">char</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">address</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">address</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"b"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-5">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-6"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-7"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-8"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">char</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"a"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-9"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"array = "</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">func</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-11"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-12"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-13">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-14"><span class="crayon-v">Output</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-15"><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">a</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec7f050064248-16"><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">a</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0022 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Why doesn&#8217;t the second example act as the first example.  As the output would be:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73f0dec86776626657" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dec86776626657-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dec86776626657-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec86776626657-1"><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">a</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec86776626657-2"><span class="crayon-t">array</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">b</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>What I&#8217;ve noticed is when passing an array by address it changes the address that the pointer points to when inside the function.  This causes the original value to never be changed.  I guess that&#8217;s just how it works.</p>
<p>[ Good question and insight.  As it turns out, pointer parameters are actually passed by value.  Consequently, if you try to change what a pointer points to inside a function, it&#8217;s the same as changing a variable locally -- as soon as you leave the function, it will revert back to what it was.  However, if you dereference the pointer and change the value of what it points to, that won&#8217;t be reverted.  If you actually want to be able to change the address that a pointer points to inside a function, the best way to do this is to pass the pointer itself by reference:</p>
<p><code>void func(char *&#038;address)</code></p>
<p>Incidentally, this line of code is dangerous:<br />
<code><br />
address = "b"<br />
</code></p>
<p>This is setting the address of the &#8220;address&#8221; variable to the address of &#8220;b&#8221;.  What is the address of &#8220;b&#8221;?  &#8220;b&#8221; isn&#8217;t a variable, so this doesn&#8217;t really make any sense.  It probably works in this case due to the way the compiler is dealing with string literals, but I certainly wouldn&#8217;t want to trust it. -Alex ]</p>
<p>Any insight on this issue?  Btw, I know that char *array is not an array but a pointer, but once again it really is an array when used with strings right?  Just different syntax right? </p>
<p>[ In C  , arrays and pointers are pretty much identical.  When you declare an array, all you&#8217;re doing is setting a pointer to the beginning of your allocated memory.  If I&#8217;m reading your above statement correctly, your understanding is correct.  This means you can do something like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73f0dec8e672341175" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dec8e672341175-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dec8e672341175-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dec8e672341175-3">3</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec8e672341175-1"><span class="crayon-t">char</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">buf</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Hello, World"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// create a static array</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec8e672341175-2"><span class="crayon-t">char</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">ptr</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">buf</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// set a pointer to that array</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dec8e672341175-3"><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">ptr</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-cn">4</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// use the pointer like an array</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>and it will print &#8216;o&#8217;. -Alex ]</p>

		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/49940bc18e5cb33696c6af3bfcf8952d?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/49940bc18e5cb33696c6af3bfcf8952d?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">weirdolino</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/#comment-30124">
		October 16, 2008 at 10:08 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/?replytocom=30124#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-30124", "30124", "respond", "111" )' aria-label='Reply to weirdolino'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I&#8217;m having trouble understanding the conclusions. Under advantages you say<br />
<cite>Because a copy of the argument is not made, it is fast, even when used with large structs or classes.</cite><br />
and under disadvantages you say<br />
<cite>Because dereferencing a pointer is slower than accessing a value directly, accessing arguments passed by address is slower than accessing arguments passed by value.</cite></p>
<p>Is passing by reference/address slower or faster than by value? Does it depend on the size of the data passed to the function?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-30168">
		<div id="div-comment-30168" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/#comment-30168">
		October 17, 2008 at 11:55 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/?replytocom=30168#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-30168", "30168", "respond", "111" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When we talk about speed and efficiency with regards to variables, we&#8217;re talking about two separate things:</p>
<p>1) The speed of creating the variable and initializing it&#8217;s values.  This cost is paid once when the variable is created, and can be significant for large classes that are copied by value.  This is why large classes are better passed by pointer or reference than by value, especially if a function is called many times.</p>
<p>2) The speed of accessing the value stored in the variable.  This cost is paid each time the variable is accessed.  Although accessing pointers and references is slower than accessing normal variables because of the dereference that takes place, in practice this is rarely a large concern unless you have some kind of loop that accesses the variable hundreds or thousands of times.</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-59753">

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/#comment-59753">
		May 1, 2009 at 8:55 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/?replytocom=59753#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-59753", "59753", "respond", "111" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When we declare a pointer, we use the * or [] syntax to let the compiler know that this variable is a pointer as opposed to a normal variable.  However, from that point forward, we can just use the variable&#8217;s name and the compiler already knows it&#8217;s a pointer.</p>
<p>So if we want to pass the array to a function that expects a pointer, all we need to do is pass the variable itself.</p>
<p>It&#8217;s the same as the following:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-9">9</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-10">10</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">printPtr</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pInt</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-c">// pInt is a pointer, so we dereference it to get it's value</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pInt</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-5"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-6">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-7"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">nX</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-8"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pX</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;nX</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// pX is a pointer that points to nX</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-9">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0de1c9316964568-10"><span class="crayon-e">printPtr</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">pX</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// we pass the pointer here</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0015 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>pX already knows it&#8217;s a pointer, so when we pass it to printPtr, we don&#8217;t need to tell the compiler that it&#8217;s a pointer again.</p>

   int *pPtr = &amp;nFive;<br />

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-59766">
		<div id="div-comment-59766" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/#comment-59766">
		May 1, 2009 at 9:40 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/?replytocom=59766#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-59766", "59766", "respond", "111" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You are correct.  We dereference a pointer to get the value of what it&#8217;s pointing at.</p>
<p>int *pPtr = &nFive; // pPtr holds the address of nFive<br />
cout << pPtr; // prints the address of nFive<br />
cout << *pPtr; // prints the value at the address of nFive, which is whatever value was assigned to nFive</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde6f018408460-1"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">SetToSix</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;pTempPtr</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde6f018408460-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde6f018408460-3"><span class="crayon-v">pTempPtr</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;nSix</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde6f018408460-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-o">!</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">formatted</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>and</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-1"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">SetToSix</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pTempPtr</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-3"><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pTempPtr</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">nSix</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dde79318486340-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Don&#8217;t they both do the same thing? Why bother with the top one (which is more complicated in my opinion) when you can just do the second one?</p>
		</div>

class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">stuff</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddd95821333970-34">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddd95821333970-35"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">PassPointerByReference4</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">stuff</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddd95821333970-36"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">stuff</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddd95821333970-37"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddd95821333970-38"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-o">!</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">formatted</span><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0067 seconds] -->
<p>The output of this program is &#8220;01134&#8221; not &#8220;01234&#8221; as you might expect. This is because in &#8220;PassPointerByValue2&#8243; only a local copy of the pointer &#8220;thing&#8221; is changed whereas in &#8220;PassPointerByReference4&#8243; the actual pointer &#8220;stuff&#8221; is changed. Because a pass by reference was used, &#8220;thing&#8221; was &#8220;stuff&#8221; not a copy of &#8220;stuff&#8221; it was &#8220;stuff&#8221;. I hope that helps you see the difference. (^.^)</p>
		</div>

class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// stuff address = y's address&nbsp;&nbsp; *stuff is whatever value in stuff address</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0dd2d4666867540-35"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span 		<p>I&#8217;d like to ask a question. In this post (7.4), you say:</p>
<p><i>Note that the length of the array must be passed in as a parameter, because arrays dont keep track of how long they are. Otherwise the PrintArray() function would not know how many elements to print.</i></p>
<p>Also, in your reply to Kukudum&#8217;s comment, you said:</p>
<p><i>You are missing the fact that arrays in C++ are really just pointers. So anArray is already a pointer! PrintArray is expecting a pointer for its first parameter, so we can pass it anArray directly.</i></p>

class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddb49664844821-15"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddb49664844821-16">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddb49664844821-17"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">function</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddb49664844821-18"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddb49664844821-19"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">sizeof</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">pnArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span 					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0028 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This prints:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73f0ddb54357237238" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0ddb54357237238-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73f0ddb54357237238-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddb54357237238-1"><span class="crayon-cn">24</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73f0ddb54357237238-2"><span class="crayon-cn">4</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0002 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Now, apparently, main() is somehow aware of the fact that anArray is an array with 6 elements while function() sees nothing more than a single address (pointer). Changing the data type yields the same result - pnArray is always 4 bytes (as pointers should be on 32-bit computers) while sizeof(anArray) returns the size of the array&#8217;s elements put together (ex. 12 bytes for short, assuming there are 6 elements).</p>
<p>So I&#8217;m wondering, why does main() consider it an array and where is this information stored?</p>
<p>By the way, regarding the PrintArray function&#8230; Wouldn&#8217;t it be better to write something like &#8221; if (anArray) PrintArray(&#8230;);&#8221; inside main() instead of making a null pointer check inside PrintArray? Time is wasted on making a function call which won&#8217;t do anything. If it makes the code too complex, you can always use an inline function.</p>
		</div>

<p>#include </p>

<p>void check(int *temp)<br />
{<br />
    printf(&#8220;\n*temp : %d\n&#8221;, *temp);<br />
    *temp = six;<br />
    printf(&#8220;\n*temp : %d\n&#8221;, *temp);<br />

<p>int main()<br />
{<br />

    printf(&#8220;\nValue in ptr : %d\n&#8221;, *ptr);<br />
    check(ptr);<br />
    printf(&#8220;\nValue in ptr : %d\n&#8221;, *ptr);<br />
    return 0;<br />
}</p>

<p>*temp : 5</p>
<p>*temp : 6</p>
<p>Value in ptr : 6</p>

		</div>
		<p>Thank so much, i used pointer like this (*&amp;pTempPtr) for my program without understanding clearly why but now i get it <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":-)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /> .</p>

		<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-251243">
		<div id="div-comment-251243" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/715ba4bf2214369eb42d99ba72870d48?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/715ba4bf2214369eb42d99ba72870d48?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">youssef dirani</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/#comment-251243">
		January 25, 2015 at 7:49 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/?replytocom=251243#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251243", "251243", "respond", "111" )' aria-label='Reply to youssef dirani'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Hello<br />
&#8220;The syntax for doing a reference to a pointer is a little strange (and easy to get backwards&#8221;<br />
What&#8217;s the meaning of &#8220;easy to get backwards&#8221;?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251245">
		<div id="div-comment-251245" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/#comment-251245">
		January 25, 2015 at 12:07 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/74-passing-arguments-by-address/?replytocom=251245#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251245", "251245", "respond", "111" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The correct syntax for a pointer reference is *&#038;pPtr.  For a non-pointer variable, you&#8217;d create a reference to it like this: &#038;nFoo.  Since a pointer is declared as *pPtr, you&#8217;d think the correct syntax for a pointer reference should be &#038;*pPtr, with the ampersand on the outside.  But it isn&#8217;t so.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
	
	</ul>
